39-- **Description:** `POST /api/agents/[id]/transfer` accepts an arbitrary `targetHostUrl` from the request body and makes an HTTP request to `${normalizedUrl}/api/agents/import` with the full exported agent data. There is no allowlist validation against known hosts. Any process on localhost (or any website via CSRF since there is no CSRF protection) can exfiltrate agent data to any URL.  
40-- **Evidence:** `app/api/agents/[id]/transfer/route.ts` lines 51-61 and 95. The only validation is non-empty check and auto-prepend of `http://`.  
41-- **Impact:** Agent configuration, message history, and working directory data can be sent to any external server. Internal network services can be probed via SSRF.  
42-- **Recommendation:** Validate `targetHostUrl` against the known hosts list from `hosts.json`. Reject URLs not in the configured peer list.  
43-  
--  
45:- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
46-- **Category:** security  
47-[Omitted long context line]  
48-- **Evidence:** `app/api/teams/route.ts` lines 14-45 -- no password check for `type` or `chiefOfStaffId` fields.  
49-- **Impact:** The governance password is rendered ineffective for controlling who can create closed teams and assign COS roles.  
50-- **Recommendation:** Either (a) require governance password when `type === 'closed'` in the creation payload, or (b) strip `type` and `chiefOfStaffId` from the creation payload and force users to use the dedicated password-protected endpoints after creation.  
51-

54-- **Category:** security  
55-- **Description:** The teams list endpoint returns ALL teams including closed teams with full member lists, COS assignments, and instructions.     10→### [CC-001] `saveTasks` return value silently ignored in `createTask` and `updateTask`  
    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/task-registry.ts:123, 177  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** logic  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** `saveTasks()` returns `false` on write failure (line 54-57), but `createTask()` (line 123) and `updateTask()` (line 177) ignore this return value and return the task as if the save succeeded. This means a caller will believe their task was created/updated when it actually was not persisted to disk. The `deleteTask()` function at line 196 has the same issue but is slightly mitigated by returning a boolean.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript  
    18→  // line 48-57: saveTasks returns boolean  
    19→  export function saveTasks(teamId: string, tasks: Task[]): boolean {  
    20→    try {  
    21→      // ...  
    22→      return true  
    23→    } catch (error) {  
    24→      console.error(...)  
    25→      return false  // <-- failure return  
    26→    }  
    27→  }  
    28→  
    29→  // line 122-124: createTask ignores return value  
    30→  tasks.push(task)  
    31→  saveTasks(data.teamId, tasks)  // <-- return value discarded  
    32→  return task                     // <-- caller thinks save succeeded  
    33→  ```  
    34→- **Fix:** Check the return value of `saveTasks()` and throw an error if it returns `false`. Since these functions are wrapped in `withLock`, an error will propagate correctly. Example: `if (!saveTasks(data.teamId, tasks)) throw new Error('Failed to persist tasks')`

    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/hooks/useTeam.ts:54-62  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** logic  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** When the PUT response is not OK (`!res.ok` on line 53), `fetchTeam()` is called on line 54 to revert the optimistic update, then `throw new Error(...)` is thrown on line 55. This throw is caught by the `catch` block on line 59, which calls `fetchTeam()` AGAIN on line 60. The result is two redundant network requests to fetch the team on every HTTP error.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→```typescript  
    18→// Line 53-62  
    19→if (!res.ok) {  
    20→  await fetchTeam()  // First revert call  
    21→  throw new Error('Failed to update team')  
    22→}  
    23→// ...  
    24→} catch (err) {  
    25→  await fetchTeam()  // Second revert call - REDUNDANT on HTTP errors  
    26→  throw err  
    27→}  
    28→```  
    29→- **Fix:** Remove `await fetchTeam()` from line 54 (inside the `!res.ok` block). The catch block on line 60 already handles reverting for ALL error cases (HTTP errors and network errors). Alternatively, remove the catch-block fetchTeam and only keep the one in the `!res.ok` branch, but then network errors would not revert. The cleanest fix:  
    30→```typescript  
    31→if (!res.ok) {  
    32→  throw new Error('Failed to update team')  // Let catch handle revert  
    33→}  
    34→```  
    35→  
    36→### [CC-002] AbortError triggers state reset to empty defaults (useGovernance.ts)

    80→- **Category:** design  
    81→- **Description:** When `updateTeam` gets a non-OK HTTP response, `fetchTeam()` is called to revert the optimistic update, then `throw new Error(...)` is thrown, which is caught by the catch block that calls `fetchTeam()` again. Two redundant network requests fire on every HTTP error.  
    82→- **Evidence:** `hooks/useTeam.ts` lines 53-62.  
    83→- **Impact:** Double network traffic on errors, potential flicker if the two fetch responses arrive at different times.  
    84→- **Recommendation:** Remove the `fetchTeam()` from inside the `!res.ok` block; let the catch block handle all revert cases.  
    85→  
    86→##### [SR-007] Message filter bypass via unresolved alias as recipientAgentId  
    87→- **Severity:** SHOULD-FIX  
    88→- **Category:** security  
    89→- **Description:** `checkMessageAllowed` compares `recipientAgentId` against UUIDs in `team.agentIds`. But `sendFromUI()` falls back to `toResolved.alias || 'unknown'` when the recipient UUID is not resolved. An alias will never match any UUID in `agentIds`, so the filter treats the recipient as "not in any closed team" and defaults to allowing the message, potentially bypassing closed-team isolation.  
    90→- **Evidence:** `lib/message-send.ts` line 158 uses alias fallback; `lib/message-filter.ts` line 53 compares against UUIDs.  
    91→- **Impact:** Messages to closed-team members could bypass governance isolation if the recipient is looked up by alias rather than UUID.  
    92→- **Recommendation:** Either block messages to unresolved recipients, resolve the alias to a UUID before calling the filter, or document this as acceptable for remote/mesh targets.  
    93→

    95→- **Severity:** SHOULD-FIX

    42→  } catch (error) {

    44→    return []  
    45→  }

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6→ * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7→ * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.

    18→export interface MessageFilterResult {

    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ *  
    35→ * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    36→ * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    37→ */  
    38→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    39→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    40→  
    41→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    42→  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    43→    return { allowed: true }  
    44→  }  
    45→  
    46→  // Single snapshot of all state — avoids redundant file reads from

   117→function parseAMPAddress(address: string): {  
   118→  name: string  
   119→  tenant: string  
   120→  provider: string  
   121→  scope?: string  
   122→} | null {  
   123→  const atIndex = address.indexOf('@')  
   124→  if (atIndex === -1) return null  
   125→  
   126→  const name = address.substring(0, atIndex)  
   127→  const domain = address.substring(atIndex + 1)  
   128→  const parts = domain.split('.')  
   129→  
   130→  if (parts.length < 2) return null  
   131→  
   132→  // Provider is always the last two domain parts (e.g. "aimaestro.local", "crabmail.ai")  
   133→  const provider = parts.slice(-2).join('.')  
   134→  const tenantParts = parts.slice(0, -2)  
   135→  
   136→  if (tenantParts.length === 0) return null  
   137→  
   138→  // Last tenant part is the tenant ID, preceding parts are scope  
   139→  const tenant = tenantParts[tenantParts.length - 1]  
   140→  const scope = tenantParts.length > 1 ? tenantParts.slice(0, -1).join('.') : undefined  
   141→  
   142→  return { name, tenant, provider, scope }  
   143→}

Loading .zprofile at 01:45:13  
     1	/**  
     2	 * Transfer Registry — manages team transfer requests  
     3	 *  
     4	 * When a COS or MANAGER tries to move an agent from a closed team  
     5	 * led by a different COS, a transfer request is created that must  
     6	 * be approved by the source team's COS before the move takes effect.  
     7	 */  
     8	  
     9	import { readFileSync, writeFileSync, mkdirSync, existsSync } from 'fs'  
    10	import os from 'os'  
    11	import path from 'path'  
    12	import { randomUUID } from 'crypto'  
    13	import type { TransferRequest, TransfersFile } from '@/types/governance'  
    14	import { withLock } from '@/lib/file-lock'  
    15	  
    16	const AIMAESTRO_DIR = path.join(os.homedir(), '.aimaestro')  
    17	const TRANSFERS_FILE = path.join(AIMAESTRO_DIR, 'governance-transfers.json')  
    18	  
    19	function ensureDir(): void {  
    20	  if (!existsSync(AIMAESTRO_DIR)) {  
    21	    mkdirSync(AIMAESTRO_DIR, { recursive: true })  
    22	  }  
    23	}  
    24	  
    25	/** Load all transfer requests from disk */  
    26	export function loadTransfers(): TransferRequest[] {  
    27	  ensureDir()  
    28	  if (!existsSync(TRANSFERS_FILE)) {  
    29	    return []  
    30	  }  
    31	  try {  
    32	    const raw = readFileSync(TRANSFERS_FILE, 'utf-8')  
    33	    const data: TransfersFile = JSON.parse(raw)  
    34	    return data.requests || []  
    35	  } catch {  
    36	    return []  
    37	  }  
    38	}  
    39	  
    40	/** Save transfer requests to disk */  
    41	function saveTransfers(requests: TransferRequest[]): void {  
    42	  ensureDir()  
    43	  const data: TransfersFile = { version: 1, requests }  
    44	  writeFileSync(TRANSFERS_FILE, JSON.stringify(data, null, 2), 'utf-8')  
    45	}  
    46

    49	  agentId: string

     1	/**  
     2	 * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3	 *  
     4	 * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5	 * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6	 * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7	 * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.  
     8	 */  
     9	  
    10	import { loadGovernance } from './governance'  
    11	import { loadTeams } from './team-registry'  
    12	  
    13	export interface MessageFilterInput {  
    14	  senderAgentId: string | null // null = mesh-forwarded message  
    15	  recipientAgentId: string  
    16	}  
    17	  
    18	export interface MessageFilterResult {  
    19	  allowed: boolean  
    20	  reason?: string  
    21	}  
    22	  
    23	/**  
    24	 * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25	 *  
    26	 * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
    27	 * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28	 * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
    29	 * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    30	 * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    31	 * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    32	 * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
    33	 * 7. Default: allowed  
    34	 *  
    35	 * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    36	 * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    37	 */  
    38	export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    39	  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    40	  
    41	  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    42	  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    43	    return { allowed: true }  
    44	  }  
    45	  
    46	  // Single snapshot of all state — avo

    24	function tasksFilePath(teamId: string): string {  
    25	  // Validate teamId is a proper UUID to prevent path traversal attacks  
    26	  // Strict UUID v4 pattern (8-4-4-4-12 hex groups) to prevent path traversal  
    27	  if (!/^[0-9a-f]{8}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{12}$/i.test(teamId)) throw new Error('Invalid team ID')  
    28	  // Defense-in-depth: use basename to strip any directory components  
    29	  return path.join(TEAMS_DIR, path.basename(`tasks-${teamId}.json`))  
    30	}  
    31	  
    32	export function loadTasks(teamId: string): Task[] {  
    33	  try {  
    34	    ensureTeamsDir()  
    35	    const filePath = tasksFilePath(teamId)  
    36	    if (!fs.existsSync(filePath)) {  
    37	      return []  
    38	    }  
    39	    const data = fs.readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8')  
    40	    const parsed: TasksFile = JSON.parse(data)  
    41	    return Array.isArray(parsed.tasks) ? parsed.tasks : []  
    42	  } catch (error) {  
    43	    console.error(`Failed to load tasks for team ${teamId}:`, error)  
    44	    return []  
    45	  }

**Result:**

Loading .zprofile at 01:45:30  
     1	/**  
     2	 * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3	 *  
     4	 * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5	 * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6	 * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7	 *  
     8	 * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9	 * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10	 */  
    11	  
    12	// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13	const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14	// Set of currently held lock names  
    15	const held = new Set<string>()  
    16	  
    17	/**  
    18	 * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19	 * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20	 */  
    21	export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22	  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23	    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24	    held.add(name)  
    25	    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26	  }  
    27	  
    28	  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29	  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30	    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    31	      locks.set(name, [])  
    32	    }  
    33	    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    34	      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    35	    })  
    36	  })  
    37	}  
    38	  
    39	/**  
    40	 * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    41	 */  
    42	function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    43	  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    44	  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    45	    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    46	    const next = queue.shift()!  
    47	    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    48	      locks.delete(name)  
    49	    }  
    50	    next()  
    51	  } else {  
    52	    // No waiters — r  

... [495 more chars truncated]  

</details>

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { checkMessageAllowed } from '@/lib/message-filter'  
     3→import { loadAgents } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
     4→  
     5→// In-memory cache: avoids re-reading governance + teams files for every agent  
     6→// on each request. TTL of 5 seconds balances freshness with performance.  
     7→const cache = new Map<string, { ids: string[]; expiresAt: number }>()  
     8→const CACHE_TTL_MS = 5_000  
     9→  
    10→export async function GET(request: NextRequest) {  
    11→  try {  
    12→    const agentId = request.nextUrl.searchParams.get('agentId')  
    13→  
    14→    if (!agentId) {  
    15→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentId query parameter is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    16→    }  
    17→  
    18→    // Check cache first  
    19→    const cached = cache.get(agentId)  
    20→    if (cached && Date.now() < cached.expiresAt) {  
    21→      return NextResponse.json({ reachableAgentIds: cached.ids })  
    22→    }  
    23→  
    24→    // Cache miss or expired — compute reachable agents  
    25→    const allAgents = loadAgents()  
    26→    const reachableAgentIds: string[] = []  
    27→  
    28→    for (const agent of allAgents) {  
    29→      if (agent.id === agentId) continue  
    30→      if (agent.deletedAt) continue  
    31→  
    32→      const result = checkMessageAllowed({  
    33→        senderAgentId: agentId,  
    34→        recipientAgentId: agent.id,  
    35→      })  
    36→  
    37→      if (result.allowed) {  
    38→        reachableAgentIds.push(agent.id)  
    39→      }  
    40→    }  
    41→  
    42→    // Store in cache with TTL  
    43→    cache.set(agentId, { ids: reachableAgentIds, expiresAt: Date.now() + CACHE_TTL_MS })  
    44→  
    45→    // Evict stale/expired entries on every cache write to prevent unbounded growth  
    46→    const now = Date.now()  
    47→    for (const [key, entry] of cache) {  
    48→      if (now >= entry.expiresAt) cache.delete(key)  
    49→    }  
    50→  
    51→    r

     1→/**  
     2→ * Resolve (approve/reject) a transfer request  
     3→ * POST - Approve or reject a pending transfer  
     4→ */  
     5→  
     6→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     7→import { getTransferRequest, resolveTransferRequest } from '@/lib/transfer-registry'  
     8→import { loadTeams, saveTeams, TeamValidationException } from '@/lib/team-registry'  
     9→import { isManager, getManagerId, isChiefOfStaffAnywhere } from '@/lib/governance'  
    10→import { getAgent } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
    11→import { notifyAgent } from '@/lib/notification-service'  
    12→import { acquireLock } from '@/lib/file-lock'  
    13→  
    14→export async function POST(  
    15→  request: NextRequest,  
    16→  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  
    17→) {  
    18→  try {  
    19→    const { id } = await params  
    20→    const body = await request.json()  
    21→    const { action, resolvedBy, rejectReason } = body  
    22→  
    23→    if (!action || !resolvedBy) {  
    24→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'action and resolvedBy are required' }, { status: 400 })  
    25→    }  
    26→    if (action !== 'approve' && action !== 'reject') {  
    27→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'action must be "approve" or "reject"' }, { status: 400 })  
    28→    }  
    29→  
    30→    // Get the transfer request  
    31→    const transferReq = getTransferRequest(id)  
    32→    if (!transferReq) {  
    33→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Transfer request not found' }, { status: 404 })  
    34→    }  
    35→    if (transferReq.status !== 'pending') {  
    36→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Transfer request is already resolved' }, { status: 409 })  
    37→    }  
    38→  
    39→    // Acquire teams lock for the entire read-validate-write cycle to prevent TOCTOU races.  
    40→    // We use acquireLock directly (instead of withLock) because we need to return

     1→/**  
     2→ * AMP v1 Route Endpoint  
     3→ *  
     4→ * POST /api/v1/route  
     5→ *  
     6→ * Routes a message to the recipient agent within the local mesh network.  
     7→ * This is the primary message-sending endpoint for AMP providers.  
     8→ *  
     9→ * Authentication:  
    10→ *   - Bearer token (API key) for direct agent requests  
    11→ *   - X-Forwarded-From header for mesh-forwarded requests from known hosts  
    12→ *  
    13→ * Delivery methods:  
    14→ *   1. Local delivery — file system inbox + tmux notification (agent on this host)  
    15→ *   2. Mesh forwarding — HTTP POST to peer host's /api/v1/route (agent on another host)  
    16→ *   3. Relay queue — store-and-forward when recipient is offline or unreachable  
    17→ *  
    18→ * External providers (e.g. crabmail.ai) are rejected with 422 — clients must  
    19→ * send directly to the external provider using its route_url from registration.  
    20→ *  
    21→ * Resolution flow:  
    22→ *   1. Mesh-forwarded request? → local-only lookup (loop guard: never re-forward)  
    23→ *   2. Explicit remote host in address? → trust it, forward directly  
    24→ *   3. Otherwise? → checkMeshAgentExists (local first, then all peers)  
    25→ *   4. Resolved remote? → forwardToHost() → queue on failure  
    26→ *   5. Resolved local? → inbox write + tmux notification  
    27→ *   6. Not found anywhere? → inbox write + relay queue

    34→ *

    36→ * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.

<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `file-lock.ts`</summary>

```json
  "limit": 100

```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14→// Set of currently held lock names  
    15→const held = new Set<string>()  
    16→  
    17→/**  
    18→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    31→      locks.set(name, [])  
    32→    }  
    33→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    34→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    35→    })  
    36→  })  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→/**  
    40→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    41→ */  
    42→function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    43→  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    44→  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    45→    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    46→    const next = queue.shift()!  
    47→    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    48→      locks.delete(name)  
    49→    }  
    50→    next()  
    51→  } else {  
    52→    // No waiters — release the lock  
    53→    hel  

... [473 more chars truncated]  

</details>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 01:45:52]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Good, `string` is assignable to `string | null`, so that is fine.  

Now let me check the lock conflict issue -- `resolveTransferRequest` uses `withLock('transfers')` and the resolve route uses `acquireLock('teams')`. But `resolveTransferRequest` writes to the transfers file under the 'transfers' lock, and the resolve route manually does the teams mutation under the 'teams' lock. Let me trace if there could be a deadlock or TOCTOU issue.  

Looking at the resolve route more carefully:  

1. `acquireLock('teams')` is acquired (line 42)  
2. `resolveTransferRequest(id, ...)` is called (line 75), which internally does `withLock('transfers', ...)`   
3. Under the 'teams' lock, teams are mutated and saved (lines 103-129)  
4. 'teams' lock is released in `finally` (line 132)  

This acquires 'teams' then 'transfers' -- need to check if there's any path that acquires them in opposite order, which would cause deadlock.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 01:46:12]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

This is important -- when `senderAgent` is null (mesh-forwarded), `senderAgent?.id` is `undefined`, and `undefined || null` is `null`. The message-filter treats `null` as "mesh-forwarded, always allowed" (Step 1, line 42-44 of message-filter.ts). This is correct behavior.

But this JSON object also includes `error` and `message` fields. Let me check if this matches the type or if there's a typing issue.  

Looking at line 579-584, this response has `id`, `status: 'failed'`, `error`, `message`. But the return type of the function is `NextResponse<AMPRouteResponse | AMPError>`. The `AMPRouteResponse` has `error?: string` and `AMPError` has `error: string` and `message: string`. So this could be either type. Let me check `AMPError`.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 01:46:35]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The `forbidden` error code exists in `AMPErrorCode`, so the type is correct.  

Now, there's an interesting issue on line 580: the response object includes `id` and `status` (from `AMPRouteResponse`), but also `error` and `message` (from `AMPError`). This is a union response body `{id, status, error, message}`. TypeScript won't actually enforce this properly since both `AMPRouteResponse` and `AMPError` are partial overlaps. Let me check if this mixed object is problematic.  

The `AMPRouteResponse` has `error?: string` and the `AMPError` has `error: AMPErrorCode`. In this response, `error: 'forbidden'` -- 'forbidden' IS a valid `AMPErrorCode`, AND 'forbidden' is assignable to `string`. So this is valid for either type in the union. Not a bug, but slightly imprecise typing. This is a NIT at best.  

Now let me check for any remaining issues. Let me verify the `getTransferRequest` outside-of-lock issue in the resolve route.  

Line 31: `getTransferRequest(id)` is called **before** `acquireLock('teams')` on line 42. However, `getTransferRequest` reads the transfers file without any lock. The check `transferReq.status !== 'pending'` on line 35 happens before the lock is acquired. Then on line 75, `resolveTransferRequest` is called under the 'teams' lock, and internally it acquires 'transfers' lock and re-checks `status !== 'pending'`. So the outside-of-lock read is just an early-exit optimization, and the real check is inside the lock. This is correct -- TOCTOU is prevented by the inner lock.  

Let me now verify the cache eviction logic in `reachable/route.ts`.  

Lines 46-49: After setting a new cache entry, it iterates and deletes expired entries. This uses `for (const [key, entry] of cache)` and deletes during iteration. In JavaScript, `Map.delete()` during a `for...of` iteration over the Map is safe (per the spec, deleting the current key is explicitly allowed). This is correct.  

However, there's a potential issue: the cache is module-level and shared across requests, and there's no lock. But since JavaScript is single-threaded (no true concurrency in Node.js event loop for synchronous code), this is safe. The `async` handler only yields at `await` points, and the cache operations are all synchronous.  

Let me check one final issue in the password route -- the `setPassword` function is async (returns Promise), and the route `await`s it. But wait -- let me re-read the password route.  

Looking at line 23 of password/route.ts: `await setPassword(password)`. The governance.ts `setPassword` returns `Promise<void>` via `withLock`. This is correct.  

Now let me check the manager route. Line 40: `agent.name || agent.alias`. Need to verify that `Agent` has both `name` and `alias` fields.  

</div>

<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `useAgents.ts`</summary>

**Result:**

   200→  return { agents: sortedAgents, stats, hostErrors }  
   201→}  
   202→  
   203→/**  
   204→ * Hook to manage agents across multiple hosts  
   205→ *  
   206→ * Fetches agents from all configured hosts (local + remote) and aggregates them.  
   207→ * Supports hybrid caching: always tries live fetch first, falls back to cache for unreachable remotes.  
   208→ */  
   209→export function useAgents() {  
   210→  const { hosts, loading: hostsLoading } = useHosts()  
   211→  const [agents, setAgents] = useState<Agent[]>([])  
   212→  const [stats, setStats] = useState<AggregatedStats | null>(null)  
   213→  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(true)  
   214→  const [error, setError] = useState<Error | null>(null)  
   215→  const [hostErrors, setHostErrors] = useState<Record<string, Error>>({})  
   216→  const hasLoadedOnce = useRef(false)  
   217→  
   218→  const loadAgents = useCallback(async () => {  
   219→    if (hosts.length === 0) {  
   220→      return  
   221→    }  
   222→  
   223→    try {  
   224→      setError(null)  
   225→  
   226→      const localHosts = hosts.filter(h => h.isSelf || isLocalhostUrl(h.url))  
   227→      const remoteHosts = hosts.filter(h => !h.isSelf && !isLocalhostUrl(h.url))  
   228→  
   229→      // Fetch local host first (fast) so the UI can render immediately  
   230→      const localResults = await Promise.all(  
   231→        localHosts.map(host => fetchHostAgents(host))  
   232→      )  
   233→  
   234→      // On first load only, show local agents right away so UI doesn't wait for remotes.  
   235→      // On subsequent refreshes, skip this to avoid replacing the full list with just local agents.

     3→ *

    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ *  
    35→ * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    36→ * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    37→ */  
    38→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    39→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    40→  
    41→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    42→  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    43→    return { allowed: true }  
    44→  }

    15→  requestingAgentId?: string // undefined = web UI request (always allowed)

    17→  
    18→export interface TeamAccessResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Determine whether the requester may access the team's resources.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Decision order:  
    27→ *  1. Web UI (no agentId)      → allowed  
    28→ *  2. Team not found           → allowed (caller handles 404)  
    29→ *  3. Team is open / untyped   → allowed  
    30→ *  4. Requester is MANAGER     → allowed  
    31→ *  5. Requester is chief-of-staff → allowed  
    32→ *  6. Requester is a member    → allowed  
    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkTeamAccess(input: TeamAccessInput): TeamAccessResult {  
    36→  // 1. Web UI requests (no X-Agent-Id header) always pass  
    37→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {  
    38→    return { allowed: true }  
    39→  }  
    40→  
    41→  // 2. Team not found — let the caller deal with 404  
    42→  const team = getTeam(input.teamId)  
    43→  if (!team) {  
    44→    return { allowed: true }  
    45→  }  
    46→  
    47→  // 3. Open teams (or teams with no explicit type) have no ACL  
    48→  if (team.type !== 'closed') {  
    49→    return { allowed: true }  
    50→  }  
    51→  
    52→  // 4. MANAGER role always has access  
    53→  if (isManager(input.requestingAgentId)) {  
    54→    return { allowed: true }  
    55→  }  
    56→  
    57→  // 5.   

... [474 more chars truncated]

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 01:49:10]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `file-lock.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/file-lock.ts"
}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14→// Set of currently held lock names  
    15→const held = new Set<string>()  
    16→  
    17→/**  
    18→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    31→      locks.set(name, [])  
    32→    }  
    33→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    34→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    35→    })  
    36→  })  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→/**  
    40→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    41→ */  
    42→function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    43→  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    44→  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    45→    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    46→    const next = queue.shift()!  
    47→    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    48→      locks.delete(name)  
    49→    }  
    50→    next()  
    51→  } else {  
    52→    // No waiters — release the lock  
    53→    hel  

... [473 more chars truncated]  

</details>

     4→ * POST /api/v1/route

     7→ * This is the primary message-sending endpoint for AMP providers.  
     8→ *  
     9→ * Authentication:

    11→ *   - X-Forwarded-From header for mesh-forwarded requests from known hosts

    19→ * send directly to the external provider using its route_url from registration.  
    20→ *

    22→ *   1. Mesh-forwarded request? → local-only lookup (loop guard: never re-forward)  
    23→ *   2. Explicit remote host in address? → trust it, forward directly  
    24→ *   3. Otherwise? → checkMeshAgentExists (local first, then all peers)  
    25→ *   4. Resolved remote? → forwardToHost() → queue on failure

   128→export async function sendFromUI(options: SendFromUIOptions): Promise<{ message: Message; notified: boolean }> {  
   129→  const { from, to, subject, content } = options  
   130→  
   131→  // Parse qualified name (identifier@host-id)  
   132→  const { identifier: toIdentifier, hostId: targetHostId } = parseQualifiedName(to)  
   133→  
   134→  // Resolve sender agent (may fail for remote senders - that's ok)  
   135→  const fromAgent = resolveAgentIdentifier(from)  
   136→

   138→  const isTargetLocal = !targetHostId || isSelf(targetHostId)  
   139→  
   140→  // Resolve recipient agent  
   141→  const toAgent = resolveAgentIdentifier(toIdentifier)  
   142→

   100→}  
   101→  
   102→// ============================================================================  
   103→// Helpers  
   104→// ============================================================================  
   105→  
   106→/**  
   107→ * Parse an AMP address into components.  
   108→ *  
   109→ * Address format: name@[scope.]tenant.provider  
   110→ * Examples:  
   111→ *   alice@rnd23blocks.aimaestro.local  → { name: "alice", tenant: "rnd23blocks", provider: "aimaestro.local" }  
   112→ *   bob@myrepo.github.rnd23blocks.aimaestro.local → { name: "bob", tenant: "rnd23blocks", provider: "aimaestro.local", scope: "myrepo.github" }  
   113→ *   carol@acme.crabmail.ai → { name: "carol", tenant: "acme", provider: "crabmail.ai" }  
   114→ *  
   115→ * Returns null if the address cannot be parsed (e.g. bare name with no @).  
   116→ */  
   117→function parseAMPAddress(address: string): {  
   118→  name: string  
   119→  tenant: string  
   120→  provider: string  
   121→  scope?: string  
   122→} | null {  
   123→  const atIndex = address.indexOf('@')  
   124→  if (atIndex === -1) return null  
   125→  
   126→  const name = address.substring(0, atIndex)  
   127→  const domain = address.substring(atIndex + 1)  
   128→  const parts = domain.split('.')  
   129→  
   130→  if (parts.length < 2) return null  
   131→  
   132→  // Provider is always the last two domain parts (e.g. "aimaestro.local", "crabmail.ai")  
   133→  const provider = parts.slice(-2).join('.')  
   134→  const tenantParts = parts.slice(0, -2)  
   135→  
   136→  if (tenantParts.length === 0) return null  
   137→  
   138→  // Last tenant part is the tenant ID, preceding parts are scope  
   139→  const tenant = tenantParts[tenantParts.length - 1]  
   140→  const scope = tenantParts.length > 1 ? tenantParts.slice(0, -1).join('.') : undefined  
   141→  
   142→  return { name, tenant, provider, scope }  
   143→}  
   144→

   146→function generateMessageId(): string {  
   147→  const tim  

... [6417 more chars truncated]

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { checkMessageAllowed } from '@/lib/message-filter'  
     3→import { loadAgents } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
     4→  
     5→// In-memory cache: avoids re-reading governance + teams files for every agent  
     6→// on each request. TTL of 5 seconds balances freshness with performance.  
     7→const cache = new Map<string, { ids: string[]; expiresAt: number }>()  
     8→const CACHE_TTL_MS = 5_000  
     9→  
    10→export async function GET(request: NextRequest) {  
    11→  try {  
    12→    const agentId = request.nextUrl.searchParams.get('agentId')  
    13→  
    14→    if (!agentId) {  
    15→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentId query parameter is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    16→    }  
    17→  
    18→    // Check cache first  
    19→    const cached = cache.get(agentId)  
    20→    if (cached && Date.now() < cached.expiresAt) {  
    21→      return NextResponse.json({ reachableAgentIds: cached.ids })  
    22→    }  
    23→  
    24→    // Cache miss or expired — compute reachable agents  
    25→    const allAgents = loadAgents()  
    26→    const reachableAgentIds: string[] = []  
    27→  
    28→    for (const agent of allAgents) {  
    29→      if (agent.id === agentId) continue  
    30→      if (agent.deletedAt) continue  
    31→  
    32→      const result = checkMessageAllowed({  
    33→        senderAgentId: agentId,  
    34→        recipientAgentId: agent.id,  
    35→      })  
    36→  
    37→      if (result.allowed) {  
    38→        reachableAgentIds.push(agent.id)  
    39→      }  
    40→    }  
    41→  
    42→    // Store in cache with TTL  
    43→    cache.set(agentId, { ids: reachableAgentIds, expiresAt: Date.now() + CACHE_TTL_MS })  
    44→  
    45→    // Evict stale/expired entries on every cache write to prevent unbounded growth  
    46→    const now = Date.now()  
    47→    for (const [key, entry] of cache) {  
    48→      if (now >= entry.expiresAt) cache.delete(key)  
    49→    }  
    50→  
    51→    r  

... [259 more chars truncated]

    18→

    30→    }  
    31→    if (status) {  
    32→      requests = requests.filter(r => r.status === status)  
    33→    }  
    34→  
    35→    return NextResponse.json({ requests })  
    36→  } catch (error) {

     3→  
     4→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
     5→  try {  
     6→    const body = await request.json()  
     7→    const { password, currentPassword } = body  
     8→  
     9→    if (!password || typeof password !== 'string' || password.length < 6) {  
    10→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Password must be at least 6 characters' }, { status: 400 })  
    11→    }  
    12→  
    13→    const config = loadGovernance()  
    14→  
    15→    // If password already set, require current password  
    16→    if (config.passwordHash) {  
    17→      if (!currentPassword || !verifyPassword(currentPassword)) {  
    18→        return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid current password' }, { status: 401 })  
    19→      }  
    20→    }  
    21→  
    22→    const isChange = !!config.passwordHash  
    23→    await setPassword(password)  
    24→  
    25→    if (isChange) {  
    26→      console.log('[governance] Password changed at', new Date().toISOString())  
    27→    } else {  
    28→      console.log('[governance] Password set at', new Date().toISOString())  
    29→    }  
    30→  
    31→    return NextResponse.json({ success: true })  
    32→  } catch (error) {  
    33→    console.error('Failed to set password:', error)  
    34→    return NextResponse.json(  
    35→      { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to set password' },  
    36→      { status: 500 }  
    37→    )  
    38→  }  
    39→}

   401→    // Client-side signing is the correct AMP pattern:  
   402→    //   - Agents own their private keys (server doesn't have them)  
   403→    //   - Client signs before sending via /v1/route  
   404→    //   - Server verifies if it has the sender's public key (optional for mesh)

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 01:51:34]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

For mesh-forwarded messages, `senderAgent` is null (line 342: `const senderAgent = isMeshForwarded ? null : getAgent(auth.agentId!)`), so `senderAgent?.id` evaluates to `null`, and `checkMessageAllowed` with `senderAgentId: null` always returns `allowed: true` (Step 1 in message-filter.ts:42). This means mesh-forwarded messages still bypass the governance filter by design. Let me check if the "forwarded messages" claim in c39394e refers to something else.  

Actually, looking at the message-filter.ts code again (line 42): null senderAgentId means "mesh-forwarded message" and always passes. This is intentional - the comment says "trust mesh peers." The forwarded message bypass fix likely refers to the `forwardFromUI` path, not mesh. Let me check if there is a `forwardFromUI` or similar function.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 01:46:15]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have all the information I need to write the audit report. Let me analyze the findings:  

**useGovernance.ts analysis:**  

1. **Line 60 - `fetchTeam` called in catch after `throw err`**: In `updateTeam` on line 60, `await fetchTeam()` is called in the catch block, but then `throw err` re-throws. The `fetchTeam()` call will execute, but if `fetchTeam()` itself rejects, the original error is lost because the unhandled rejection from `fetchTeam()` will propagate instead. Wait - actually, `fetchTeam()` has its own try/catch that sets state, so it won't reject. Let me re-read... Yes, `fetchTeam` on line 19-30 catches its own errors. So this is fine.  

2. **Line 54 - Double optimistic revert in updateTeam**: On line 54, when `res.ok` is false, `fetchTeam()` is called to revert, then `throw new Error(...)` is thrown, which is caught by the catch on line 59, which calls `fetchTeam()` AGAIN. This is a double-revert -- fetchTeam is called twice on HTTP errors. This is a CONFIRMED bug (wasted network call).  

3. **Line 70 - `refresh` in catch block on line 90**: The outer `.catch()` in `refresh` resets state to safe defaults. But the individual `.catch()` calls on lines 70, 74, 78 already provide default fallback values. So if one fetch fails but the others succeed, the individual catch handles it. If the `.then()` handler on line 80 itself throws, the outer `.catch()` on line 90 would reset everything. This seems correct.  

4. **Line 66-101 - `refresh` is a non-async function returning void but performs async work**: The `refresh` function in the interface (line 20) has signature `(signal?: AbortSignal) => void`. The implementation creates a Promise chain but doesn't return it. This means callers calling `refresh()` after mutations (lines 121, 140, 159, 197, 234, 253, 272) cannot await the refresh completion. The state updates from refresh may not be visible to subsequent code. However, since these are all fire-and-forget from the UI perspective (the component re-renders when state changes), this is acceptable but worth noting.  

5. **Line 81 - Abort check only in `.then()`**: If the signal is aborted after the fetches complete but before `.then()` runs, the state is not updated (good). But there's no abort check in the `.catch()` on line 90 or `.finally()` on line 99. If the fetch is aborted, it throws an `AbortError` which is caught by the `.catch()`, which resets state to defaults. This means aborting a request causes a reset to empty state, which may flash the UI briefly before the new request's data arrives. This is a CONFIRMED issue.  

6. **Line 249 - `requestedBy: agentId`**: The `agentId` parameter could be `null` (from the hook signature `agentId: string | null`). This would send `requestedBy: null` in the request body. The `TransferRequest` type says `requestedBy: string` (not nullable). So this is a type mismatch when `agentId` is null. CONFIRMED.  

7. **Line 268 - `resolvedBy: agentId`**: Same issue as above -- `agentId` could be null but `resolv  

... [1217 more chars truncated]

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team Resource ACL — checks whether an agent (or web UI request)  
     3→ * is allowed to access a given team's resources.  
     4→ *  
     5→ * Open teams (type undefined or 'open') impose no restrictions.  
     6→ * Closed teams restrict access to the manager, chief-of-staff,  
     7→ * and team members only.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { isManager } from './governance'  
    11→import { getTeam } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface TeamAccessInput {  
    14→  teamId: string  
    15→  requestingAgentId?: string // undefined = web UI request (always allowed)  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface TeamAccessResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Determine whether the requester may access the team's resources.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Decision order:  
    27→ *  1. Web UI (no agentId)      → allowed  
    28→ *  2. Team not found           → allowed (caller handles 404)  
    29→ *  3. Team is open / untyped   → allowed  
    30→ *  4. Requester is MANAGER     → allowed  
    31→ *  5. Requester is chief-of-staff → allowed  
    32→ *  6. Requester is a member    → allowed  
    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkTeamAccess(input: TeamAccessInput): TeamAccessResult {  
    36→  // 1. Web UI requests (no X-Agent-Id header) always pass  
    37→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {  
    38→    return { allowed: true }  
    39→  }  
    40→  
    41→  // 2. Team not found — let the caller deal with 404  
    42→  const team = getTeam(input.teamId)  
    43→  if (!team) {  
    44→    return { allowed: true }  
    45→  }  
    46→  
    47→  // 3. Open teams (or teams with no explicit type) have no ACL  
    48→  if (team.type !== 'closed') {  
    49→    return { allowed: true }  
    50→  }  
    51→  
    52→  // 4. MANAGER role always has access  
    53→  if (isManager(input.requestingAgentId)) {  
    54→    return { allowed: true }  
    55→  }  
    56→  
    57→  // 5.   

... [474 more chars truncated]  

</details>

   307→    const teams = loadTeams()  
   308→    const filtered = teams.filter(t => t.id !== id)  
   309→    if (filtered.length === teams.length) return false  
   310→    saveTeams(filtered)  
   311→    // Clean up orphaned task file for the deleted team  
   312→    // Defense-in-depth: validate UUID format before constructing file path to prevent path traversal  
   313→    if (/^[0-9a-f]{8}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{12}$/i.test(id)) {  
   314→      const taskFile = path.join(TEAMS_DIR, path.basename(`tasks-${id}.json`))  
   315→      try { if (fs.existsSync(taskFile)) fs.unlinkSync(taskFile) } catch { /* ignore */ }  
   316→    }  
   317→    return true  
   318→  })  
   319→}  
   320→

     1→/**

    14→import { Host, HostsConfig } from '@/types/host'  
    15→import fs from 'fs'  
    16→import path from 'path'  
    17→import os from 'os'  
    18→  
    19→// File lock state  
    20→let lockHeld = false  
    21→const lockQueue: Array<{ resolve: () => void; reject: (err: Error) => void }> = []  
    22→const LOCK_TIMEOUT = 5000 // 5 second timeout for acquiring lock  
    23→  
    24→/**  
    25→ * Acquire a lock for file operations  
    26→ */  
    27→async function acquireLock(): Promise<void> {  
    28→  if (!lockHeld) {  
    29→    lockHeld = true  
    30→    return  
    31→  }  
    32→  
    33→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
    34→    const timeout = setTimeout(() => {  
    35→      const index = lockQueue.findIndex(item => item.resolve === resolve)  
    36→      if (index !== -1) {  
    37→        lockQueue.splice(index, 1)  
    38→      }  
    39→      reject(new Error('Lock acquisition timeout'))  
    40→    }, LOCK_TIMEOUT)  
    41→  
    42→    lockQueue.push({  
    43→      resolve: () => {  
    44→        clearTimeout(timeout)  
    45→        resolve()  
    46→      },  
    47→      reject: (err: Error) => {  
    48→        clearTimeout(timeout)  
    49→        reject(err)  
    50→      },  
    51→    })  
    52→  })  
    53→}  
    54→  
    55→/**  
    56→ * Release the lock and process next in queue  
    57→ */  
    58→function releaseLock(): void {  
    59→  if (lockQueue.length > 0) {  
    60→    const next = lockQueue.shift()  
    61→    if (next) {  
    62→      next.resolve()  
    63→    }  
    64→  } else {  
   

... [1338 more chars truncated]  

</details>

  3504→+export function useGovernance(agentId: string | null): GovernanceState {  
  3505→+  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(true)  
  3506→+  const [hasPassword, setHasPassword] = useState(false)  
  3507→+  const [hasManager, setHasManager] = useState(false)  
  3508→+  const [managerId, setManagerId] = useState<string | null>(null)  
  3509→+  const [managerName, setManagerName] = useState<string | null>(null)  
  3510→+  const [allTeams, setAllTeams] = useState<Team[]>([])  
  3511→+  const [pendingTransfers, setPendingTransfers] = useState<TransferRequest[]>([])  
  3512→+  
  3513→+  // Derive governance role from current state  
  3514→+  const agentRole: GovernanceRole = useMemo(() => {  
  3515→+    if (!agentId) return 'normal'  
  3516→+    if (managerId === agentId) return 'manager'  
  3517→+    // team.type is now required per types/team.ts  
  3518→+    const isCOS = allTeams.some(  
  3519→+      (t) => t.type === 'closed' && t.chiefOfStaffId === agentId  
  3520→+    )  
  3521→+    if (isCOS) return 'chief-of-staff'  
  3522→+    return 'normal'  
  3523→+  }, [agentId, managerId, allTeams])

    10→### [CC-001] `saveTasks` return value silently ignored in `createTask` and `updateTask`  
    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/task-registry.ts:123, 177  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** logic  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** `saveTasks()` returns `false` on write failure (line 54-57), but `createTask()` (line 123) and `updateTask()` (line 177) ignore this return value and return the task as if the save succeeded. This means a caller will believe their task was created/updated when it actually was not persisted to disk. The `deleteTask()` function at line 196 has the same issue but is slightly mitigated by returning a boolean.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript

    23→    } catch (error) {

    25→      return false  // <-- failure return  
    26→    }  
    27→  }  
    28→  
    29→  // line 122-124: createTask ignores return value  
    30→  tasks.push(task)  
    31→  saveTasks(data.teamId, tasks)  // <-- return value discarded  
    32→  return task                     // <-- caller thinks save succeeded  
    33→  ```  
    34→- **Fix:** Check the return value of `saveTasks()` and throw an error if it returns `false`. Since these functions are wrapped in `withLock`, an error will propagate correctly. Example: `if (!saveTasks(data.teamId, tasks)) throw new Error('Failed to persist tasks')`

    19→- **Description:** The `getTransferRequest(id)` call on line 31 and the status check on line 35 happen **before** the `acquireLock('teams')` on line 42. While this is functionally correct (it's a read-only early-exit optimization, and the real concurrency-safe check is inside `resolveTransferRequest` which uses its own 'transfers' lock), it creates a subtle TOCTOU window: between the pre-lock read and the post-lock `resolveTransferRequest`, a concurrent request could resolve the same transfer. The inner `resolveTransferRequest` handles this correctly by returning `null` on double-resolve, and the route returns 409. However, there is a wasted lock acquisition and team-loading cycle in the race case. This is a performance nit, not a correctness bug, because the second check inside `resolveTransferRequest` is authoritative.

    27→  const releaseLock = await acquireLock('teams')  
    28→  // Line 75: Second check inside resolveTransferRequest (with 'transfers' lock)  
    29→  resolved = await resolveTransferRequest(id, ...)

    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/components/governance/GovernancePasswordDialog.tsx:35-40  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** logic  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** The `useEffect` for the Escape key handler has a dependency array of `[isOpen]`, but it captures `handleClose` from the closure at the time the effect runs. `handleClose` itself references `submitting` state. If `submitting` changes after the effect has registered the keydown listener, pressing Escape will use a stale `submitting` value (always the value from when the effect ran). This means pressing Escape while a submission is in progress could close the dialog despite the `if (submitting) return` guard in `handleClose`.  
    16→- **Evidence:**

    24→}, [isOpen])  // Missing handleClose dependency  
    25→  
    26→// handleClose references `submitting` state:  
    27→const handleClose = () => {  
    28→  if (submitting) return  // stale closure - submitting is always false from initial render  
    29→  onClose()  
    30→  ...  
    31→}  
    32→```  
    33→- **Fix:** Either add `handleClose` (wrapped in `useCallback`) to the dependency array, or add `submitting` to the dependency array and inline the check: `if (e.key === 'Escape' && !submitting) handleClose()`. The recommended fix is to wrap `handleClose` in `useCallback`

The transfer-registry source file genuinely uses named imports, so its mock pattern is actually correct for its specific source file. However, the mock does NOT wrap the functions in a `default` property, meaning if Vitest's module resolution for `fs` aliases named exports through `default`, this could break. In practice, Node's `fs` module exports both named and default, and Vitest's mock factory replaces the entire module, so providing named exports directly is valid for destructured imports. **After full trace: this is actually correct and matches the source import style.     15→- **Description:** When the PUT response is not OK (`!res.ok` on line 53), `fetchTeam()` is called on line 54 to revert the optimistic update, then `throw new Error(...)` is thrown on line 55.     16→- **Evidence:**

    24→} catch (err) {  
    25→  await fetchTeam()  // Second revert call - REDUNDANT on HTTP errors  
    26→  throw err  
    27→}  
    28→```  
    29→- **Fix:** Remove `await fetchTeam()` from line 54 (inside the `!res.ok` block). The catch block on line 60 already handles reverting for ALL error cases (HTTP errors and network errors). Alternatively, remove the catch-block fetchTeam and only keep the one in the `!res.ok` branch, but then network errors would not revert. The cleanest fix:  
    30→```typescript  
    31→if (!res.ok) {  
    32→  throw new Error('Failed to update team')  // Let catch handle revert  
    33→}  
    34→```

     1→#!/bin/bash  
     2→# AI Maestro - Version Bump Script  
     3→# Centralizes version management across all files  
     4→#  
     5→# Usage:  
     6→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh patch    # 0.17.12 -> 0.17.13  
     7→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh minor    # 0.17.12 -> 0.18.0  
     8→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh major    # 0.17.12 -> 1.0.0  
     9→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh 0.18.0   # Set specific version  
    10→  
    11→set -e  
    12→  
    13→# Colors  
    14→RED='\033[0;31m'  
    15→GREEN='\033[0;32m'  
    16→YELLOW='\033[1;33m'  
    17→CYAN='\033[0;36m'  
    18→NC='\033[0m'  
    19→  
    20→# Get script directory and project root  
    21→SCRIPT_DIR="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")" && pwd)"  
    22→PROJECT_ROOT="$(dirname "$SCRIPT_DIR")"  
    23→  
    24→# Read current version from version.json  
    25→VERSION_FILE="$PROJECT_ROOT/version.json"  
    26→if [ ! -f "$VERSION_FILE" ]; then  
    27→    echo -e "${RED}Error: version.json not found${NC}"  
    28→    exit 1  
    29→fi  
    30→  
    31→CURRENT_VERSION=$(grep -o '"version": *"[^"]*"' "$VERSION_FILE" | cut -d'"' -f4)  
    32→echo -e "${CYAN}Current version: ${CURRENT_VERSION}${NC}"  
    33→  
    34→# Parse current version  
    35→IFS='.' read -r MAJOR MINOR PATCH <<< "$CURRENT_VERSION"  
    36→  
    37→# Determine new version  
    38→case "$1" in  
    39→    patch)  
    40→        PATCH=$((PATCH + 1))  
    41→        NEW_VERSION="${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH}"  
    42→        ;;  
    43→    minor)  
    44→        MINOR=$((MINOR + 1))  
    45→        PATCH=0  
    46→        NEW_VERSION="${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH}"  
    47→        ;;  
    48→    major)  
    49→        MAJOR=$((MAJOR + 1))  
    50→        MINOR=0  
    51→        PATCH=0  
    52→        NEW_VERSION="${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH}"  
    53→        ;;  
    54→    "")  
    55→        echo ""  
    56→        echo "Usage: $0 <patch|minor|major|version>"  
    57→        echo ""  
    58→        echo "Examples:"  
    59→        echo "  $0 patch    # ${CURRENT_VERSION} -> ${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.$((PATCH + 1

    12→## Now (Next Release - v0.5.0)  
    13→  
    14→### 1. Memory Optimization & Leak Prevention  
    15→  
    16→**Status:** Planned  
    17→**Priority:** High  
    18→**Effort:** Small (1 day)  
    19→**Version:** v0.5.0  
    20→  
    21→**Problem:**  
    22→After comprehensive memory analysis, several potential memory leaks and inefficiencies were identified:  
    23→- Large terminal scrollback buffers (50,000 lines × 11 terminals = 550,000 lines, ~110-200 MB)  
    24→- Refresh timeouts not cleaned up on unmount (minor leak)  
    25→- Unbounded message buffer growth during slow initialization (edge case)  
    26→- Console logging accumulation when DevTools is open (20-50 MB over hours)  
    27→- No Node.js heap size limits (can crash with OOM)  
    28→  
    29→**Current Memory Usage (Baseline):**  
    30→- Server: 227 MB RSS (healthy)  
    31→- Browser: 500-800 MB (acceptable but can be optimized)  
    32→- 11 active sessions, 2+ days runtime  
    33→  
    34→**Reference:** See `docs/MEMORY-ANALYSIS.md` for detailed analysis.  
    35→  
    36→---  
    37→  
    38→**Quick Wins (High Priority):**  
    39→

    41→```typescript  
    42→// hooks/useTerminal.ts:144  
    43→scrollback: 10000,  // Reduce from 50,000 → 10,000 lines  
    44→```  
    45→  
    46→**Impact:** Saves ~80-100 MB browser memory (11 terminals)

    49→- Most users don't need 50,000 lines in xterm.js buffer

   316→export function useMessageNotifications(sessionName: string) {  
   317→  useEffect(() => {  
   318→    const ws = new WebSocket(`ws://localhost:23000/term?name=${sessionName}`);  
   319→  
   320→    ws.onmessage = (event) => {  
   321→      const msg = JSON.parse(event.data);  
   322→  
   323→      if (msg.type === 'message:read') {  
   324→        // Update UI: show read receipt

   327→        // Show toast notification

   329→          description: `Read at ${new Date(msg.data.readAt).toLocaleTimeString()}`  
   330→        });  
   331→      }  
   332→    };  
   333→  
   334→    return () => ws.close();  
   335→  }, [sessionName]);  
   336→}  
   337→```
